<div id="review_115130047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115130047" />
    <a title="Jenine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4105293-jenine"><img alt="Jenine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541074974p2/4105293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115130047?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenine" href="/user/show/4105293-jenine">Jenine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer115130047&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115130047" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6138158765999539189">I would like to rate this 3.5 stars...why oh why don't you let me do halfs goodreads?? <br/> <br/>I was so excited to read this but also kinda anxious at the same time. Second book syndrome. Love triangle, girl and boy not communicating, keeping secrets, boy not being around, girl being down right dumb ala cresendo, torment, new moon etc.<br/><br/>I can't say I was wrong about this but I did still like it. I love Bree's writing style and while it was slow at points I knew it was going to go out with a bang. I misse</span>
  <span id="freeText6138158765999539189" style="display:none">I would like to rate this 3.5 stars...why oh why don't you let me do halfs goodreads?? <br /> <br />I was so excited to read this but also kinda anxious at the same time. Second book syndrome. Love triangle, girl and boy not communicating, keeping secrets, boy not being around, girl being down right dumb ala cresendo, torment, new moon etc.<br /><br />I can't say I was wrong about this but I did still like it. I love Bree's writing style and while it was slow at points I knew it was going to go out with a bang. I missed Daniel, it seems like we barely ever saw him. I liked the fact that April got brought back into things and that she actually knew what was going on. She did annoy me at times but did the right thing in the end by telling Gabriel about Grace and Talbot. I thought I knew what was going to happen as soon as Talbot arrived, he was the bad guy, he was one of the shadow kings, Daniels father was somehow involved. But no....couldnt be that simple now could it? By the end my head was spinning. Judes evil. No he's not. Talbots evil. Hang on maybe not. Definately Jude....maybe Talbot. AGHH. So Talbot had bad intentions in the first place that was obvious, having Grace sneak out, lie, and take off her moon stone. No alarm bells going off for her?? Of course not. And the damn wolf. How daft is this girl? I missed the strong, smart, confident Grace from the Dark Divine hopefully she will come back. She didn't once question that this strange voice in her head that was never there before could be the wolf until someone points it out? I wonder at what stage Talbot stopped manipulating Grace and started to fall for her? And does he know Caleb is the one who was behind the attack on his family?<br /><br />Anyway It might sound as though I didn't like the book, I did. I liked how Don, Talbot and Gabriel as well as Caleb were all linked. I like how things were left to lead into the final book. I loved how the title the Lost Saint could be Gabriel or Talbot. I liked original minor chartacters having small parts to play as well such as Pete and Mischka.<br /><br />I still have serious doubts about Jude, he obviously has some good in him to be calling Grace and contacting April but I think that was just when Jude broke free from the wolf. He did nothing to try and help Grace when her life was on the line. Bad dog. LOL<br /><br />The ending was good. Daniel becoming the true alpa but now possibly being stuck as a wolf? (shiver anyone?) Of course it will all work out in the end, It always does...well most of the time. Maybe. I hope so.<br /><br />Daniel proposing!!! *thud*<br /><br /><i>"Do you think after Trenton, we could get married and settle down in an apartment in New York City or somewhere? I could be an industrial designer, and you could fight crime like a part-time ninja assassin."</i><br /><br />I especially liked the ninja bit....<s>and I must say I have to agree with Caleb on this one that some skin would have been nice &gt;.&gt;<br /> </s><br />The real Grace did come through in the end, willing to sacrifice herself to save Daniel and her family. Having the strength to fight her inner demon when the wolves where attacking her. She redeemed herself in my eyes.<br /><br />All though I don't like or trust Talbot this cracked me up "What did you think, we were going to take them all out for ice cream and buy them puppies?"<br /><br />Oh and wolf Grace trying to have her evil way with poor defenseless Daniel?? BOL!! Loved it!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6138158765999539189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Dngv23iSiN8LieB4UubvXQCmm5mTR0RJlcQWaX7MQTiB/dZvMqHFLOmJxvJ/XOKkufcAdmaySZFDKEA9IVvygQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('atwASVaJG7Ue4K83WCoPnLVKhObrYuY+ahkw/lL0ofjlWfn9HLpWRvzgib11kAJlDBsfCR6X6+a89WaqDWMSQQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer4838724731552825607">The Short: Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner-city teens from Philadelphia and New York. She currently lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband, two young sons, and her beloved TiVo. The Dark Divine is Bree's debut novel.<br/><br/>The Long: As a kid, Bree would staple folded papers to make her own </span>
  <span id="freeText4838724731552825607" style="display:none">The Short: Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner-city teens from Philadelphia and New York. She currently lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband, two young sons, and her beloved TiVo. The Dark Divine is Bree's debut novel.<br /><br />The Long: As a kid, Bree would staple folded papers to make her own "novels." As a teen, she wrote stories in notebooks while her friends waited for the next page to be finished. Her teachers told her she should be a writer. But Bree thought only special people could be writers, so as the years past, she settled into the idea of becoming a lawyer or something else just as ordinary.<br /><br />Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner city teens from Philadelphia and New York. With a renewed passion for story, and the young adult audience, she returned to Brigham Young University, filled her schedule with creative writing and literature classes, and started writing stories again. But regular life kicked in, and she soon found herself married with a new baby, working full-time, and with very little writing done.<br /><br />That’s when the universe threw a pick-up truck in her path. The car accident left Bree with an understanding that life was too short to not do what you absolutely love. A few days later, her husband brought home a used laptop computer, placed it by her bedside, and said, “You’d better start writing.” Her life has never been the same since. <br /><br />In a moment of karmic perfection, Bree received the offer to purchase The Dark Divine on the 6th anniversary of the car accident that put her back on the path to becoming an author.</span>
